R: Jane was a professor teaching piano to students.
S: Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book.
X: Two of Jane's students were early for their lessons.
Y: None of Jane's students had a lesson that day.
A: Let's think step by step.Observation R tells us that Jane is a professor teaching piano to students. Hypothesis X explains this observation by stating that two of Jane's students were early for their lessons. This hypothesis is consistent with the observation and provides a plausible explanation for it. 

Observation S tells us that Jane spent the morning sipping coffee and reading a book. Hypothesis Y explains this observation by stating that none of Jane's students had a lesson that day. This hypothesis is also consistent with the observation and provides a plausible explanation for it. 

Therefore, both hypotheses X and Y have the power to explain the observations, but they explain different observations. Hypothesis X explains observation R, while hypothesis Y explains observation S. It is not possible to determine which hypothesis has more power to explain the observations without additional information or evidence. 
Therefore, the answer is that both hypotheses have equal power to explain their respective observations.

Y: May aced all of her classes her freshman year.
A: Let's think step by step.Hypothesis X explains observation R (May being accepted to college in Fredonia) by suggesting that May missed her family and boyfriend, which could have motivated her to apply to a college closer to home. However, hypothesis X does not explain observation S (May dropping out of school) very well. It is possible that May dropped out because she missed her family and boyfriend, but there could be other reasons as well.

On the other hand, hypothesis Y explains observation S (May dropping out of school) very well by suggesting that May struggled academically and could not keep up with the demands of college. However, hypothesis Y does not explain observation R (May being accepted to college in Fredonia) very well. It is possible that May aced all of her classes her freshman year, but there could be other reasons why she was accepted to college in Fredonia.

Therefore, neither hypothesis X nor Y has more power to explain both observations R and S. It is possible that there is another hypothesis that can better explain both observations, or that there are multiple factors contributing to May's decisions and actions. 
Therefore, the answer is that neither hypothesis X nor Y has more power to explain the observations.

S: Hannah decided she loved her new job.
X: Her coworkers were welcoming, and her work was easy.
Y: Hannah went in and had a ok first day.
A: Let's think step by step.First, we need to determine which hypothesis, X or Y, better explains the observation R (Today was the day Hannah began her new job). Both hypotheses seem to be equally plausible explanations for this observation, as both suggest that Hannah started a new job. Therefore, neither hypothesis has more power to explain observation R.

Next, we need to determine which hypothesis, X or Y, better explains the observation S (Hannah decided she loved her new job). Hypothesis X (Her coworkers were welcoming, and her work was easy) seems to be a more plausible explanation for this observation than hypothesis Y (Hannah went in and had an ok first day). If Hannah's coworkers were welcoming and her work was easy, it would make sense that she would enjoy her new job. Therefore, hypothesis X has more power to explain observation S. 
Therefore, the answer is hypothesis X.
